<a id="yuangaohuanzuo2022FItPoEB3PAAFASM"></a>
### <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/openaccess.svg"><img src="ico/wm/openaccess.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture> <a href="https://github.com/dan-auer/3dcp.fyi/blob/main/dat/3dcp.fyi.bib#L107034-L107068" title="Get the BibTeX Entry"><picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/bibtex.svg"><img src="ico/wm/bibtex.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a> <a href="https://doi.org/10.3390/ma15051969" title="DOI" ><picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/doi.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/doi.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a> <a href="https://crossmark.crossref.org/dialog/?doi=10.3390/ma15051969&domain=pdf" title="Crossmark" ><picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/crossmark.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/crossmark.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a> <a href="https://www.mdpi.com/1996-1944/15/5/1969/pdf?version=1646644267" title="Get the *.pdf via unpaywall.com" ><picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/down.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/down.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a> Factors Influencing the Properties of Extrusion-Based 3D-Printed Alkali-Activated Fly Ash-Slag Mortar (2022-03)
<a href="https://orcid.org/0000-0003-4375-944X">Qiang <b>Yuan</b> <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/orcid.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/orcid.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a>,
Chao <b>Gao</b>,
<a href="https://orcid.org/0000-0003-1023-6159">Tingjie <b>Huang</b> <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/orcid.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/orcid.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a>,
Shenghao <b>Zuo</b>,
Hao <b>Yao</b>,
Kai <b>Zhang</b>,
Yanling <b>Huang</b>,
Jing <b>Liu</b><br>Journal Article – Materials, Vol. 15, No. 5
<details><summary>Abstract</summary>The mix proportioning of extrusion-based 3D-printed cementitious material should balance printability and hardened properties. This paper investigated the effects of three key mix proportion parameters of 3D-printed alkali-activated fly ash/slag (3D-AAFS) mortar, i.e., the sand to binder (s/b) ratio, fly ash/ground granulated blast-furnace slag (FA/GGBS) ratio, and silicate modulus (Ms) of the activator, on extrudability, buildability, interlayer strength, and drying shrinkage. The results showed that the loss of extrudability and the development of buildability were accelerated by increasing the s/b ratio, decreasing the FA/GGBS ratio, or using a lower Ms activator. A rise in the s/b ratio improved the interlayer strength and reduces the drying shrinkage. Although increasing the FA/GGBS mass ratio from 1 to 3 led to a reduction of 35% in the interlayer bond strength, it decreased the shrinkage strain by half. A larger silicate modulus was beneficial to the interlayer bond strength, but it made shrinkage more serious. Moreover, a simple centroid design method was developed for optimizing the mix proportion of 3D-AAFS mortar to simultaneously meet the requirements of printability and hardened properties.</details>

<a id="zhandengchenzhan2022PtSYSo3PCBoFoPaToEPL"></a>
### <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/closedaccess.svg"><img src="ico/wm/closedaccess.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture> <a href="https://github.com/dan-auer/3dcp.fyi/blob/main/dat/3dcp.fyi.bib#L108413-L108445" title="Get the BibTeX Entry"><picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/bibtex.svg"><img src="ico/wm/bibtex.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a> <a href="https://doi.org/10.1016/j.cemconcomp.2022.104494" title="DOI" ><picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/doi.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/doi.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a> <a href="https://crossmark.crossref.org/dialog/?doi=10.1016/j.cemconcomp.2022.104494&domain=pdf" title="Crossmark" ><picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/crossmark.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/crossmark.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a> <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/blank.svg"><img src="ico/wm/blank.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture> Predicting the Static Yield Stress of 3D Printable Concrete Based on Flowability of Paste and Thickness of Excess Paste Layer (2022-03)
<a href="https://orcid.org/0000-0002-4947-4077">Chao <b>Zhang</b> <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/orcid.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/orcid.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a>,
Zhicong <b>Deng</b>,
Chun <b>Chen</b>,
<a href="https://orcid.org/0000-0003-1864-2258">Yamei <b>Zhang</b> <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/orcid.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/orcid.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a>,
<a href="https://orcid.org/0000-0002-4685-7064">Viktor <b>Mechtcherine</b> <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/orcid.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/orcid.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a>,
Zhengming <b>Sun</b><br>Journal Article – Cement and Concrete Composites, Vol. 129
<details><summary>Abstract</summary>Static yield stress is the most vital rheological parameter affecting the printability of concrete for additive manufacturing technologies based on layered extrusion. According to the theoretical analysis on the relationship between the static yield stress and the concrete composition, the components of 3D printable concrete (3DPC) can be divided into paste phase and aggregate phase. Within this context, the influence of paste composition and aggregate content on the static yield stress of 3DPC was investigated in this research. It is found that the static yield stress of 3DPC is proportional to the static/dynamic yield stress of its corresponding paste and the aggregate content, separately. Additionally, it is proved that the flowability of paste significantly depends on its static/dynamic yield stress, no matter which type of rheological modifier agents is applied. Based on the experimental results, a modified Coussot model was established to predict the static yield stress of 3DPC, allowing for the flowability of paste and the thickness of excess paste layer as crucial parameters.</details>

<a id="zhanzhanyangliu2022HPaDoLS3PCBM"></a>
### <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/openaccess.svg"><img src="ico/wm/openaccess.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture> <a href="https://github.com/dan-auer/3dcp.fyi/blob/main/dat/3dcp.fyi.bib#L110066-L110096" title="Get the BibTeX Entry"><picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/bibtex.svg"><img src="ico/wm/bibtex.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a> <a href="https://doi.org/10.1617/s11527-022-01919-7" title="DOI" ><picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/doi.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/doi.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a> <a href="https://crossmark.crossref.org/dialog/?doi=10.1617/s11527-022-01919-7&domain=pdf" title="Crossmark" ><picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/crossmark.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/crossmark.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a> <a href="https://link.springer.com/content/pdf/10.1617/s11527-022-01919-7.pdf" title="Get the *.pdf via unpaywall.com" ><picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/down.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/down.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a> Hardened Properties and Durability of Large-Scale 3D Printed Cement-Based Materials: Correction (2022-03)
<a href="https://orcid.org/0000-0003-4668-1553">Yu <b>Zhang</b> <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/orcid.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/orcid.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a>,
<a href="https://orcid.org/0000-0001-5630-4570">Yunsheng <b>Zhang</b> <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/orcid.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/orcid.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a>,
<a href="https://orcid.org/0000-0002-6910-2596">Lin <b>Yang</b> <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/orcid.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/orcid.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a>,
<a href="https://orcid.org/0000-0003-2023-2741">Guojian <b>Liu</b> <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/orcid.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/orcid.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a>,
<a href="https://orcid.org/0000-0003-3561-8057">Yidong <b>Chen</b> <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/orcid.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/orcid.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a>,
<a href="https://orcid.org/0000-0002-3361-2957">Shiwei <b>Yu</b> <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/orcid.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/orcid.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a>,
<a href="https://orcid.org/0000-0002-3801-637X">Hongjian <b>Du</b> <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/orcid.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/orcid.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a><br>Journal Article – Materials and Structures, Vol. 55, No. 2
<details><summary>Abstract</summary>This study systematically investigates the hardened properties, durability and void distribution of large-scale 3D printed cement-based materials (3DPC). Experimental results indicate that 3DPC has higher compressive and flexural strengths, lower drying shrinkage, better resistance against sulfate attack and carbonation than mold-cast cement-based materials, but lower resistance to frost damage and chloride ion penetration. Computed tomography scanning reveals that voids in 3DPC are strongly oriented along the printing direction. Furthermore, the voids are much more inter-connected and even continuous among the printed filaments. This unique void distribution is the origin of anisotropy for 3DPC and can explain the determined directional dependency of mechanical strengths and durability performance. Along the printing direction, the more connected voids render more channels for gas and liquid to penetrate into 3DPC.</details>

### <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/closedaccess.svg"><img src="ico/wm/closedaccess.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture> <a href="https://github.com/dan-auer/3dcp.fyi/blob/main/dat/3dcp.fyi.bib#L110733-L110763" title="Get the BibTeX Entry"><picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/bibtex.svg"><img src="ico/wm/bibtex.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a> <a href="https://doi.org/10.1016/j.autcon.2022.104199" title="DOI" ><picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/doi.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/doi.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a> <a href="https://crossmark.crossref.org/dialog/?doi=10.1016/j.autcon.2022.104199&domain=pdf" title="Crossmark" ><picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/crossmark.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/crossmark.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a> <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/blank.svg"><img src="ico/wm/blank.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture> Effect of Spiral Blade Geometry on 3D-Printed Concrete Rheological Properties and Extrudability Using Discrete Event Modeling (2022-03)
<a href="https://orcid.org/0000-0002-3690-5018">Peng <b>Zhi</b> <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/orcid.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/orcid.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a>,
<a href="https://orcid.org/0000-0002-2033-0520">Yuching <b>Wu</b> <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/orcid.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/orcid.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a>,
Qianfan <b>Yang</b>,
Xiangrui <b>Kong</b>,
<a href="https://orcid.org/0000-0003-1287-1199">Jianzhuang <b>Xiao</b> <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/orcid.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/orcid.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a><br>Journal Article – Automation in Construction, Vol. 137
<details><summary>Abstract</summary>Sizes and shapes of spiral blades have a great influence on 3D printable concrete construction. This study is presented to answer two research questions: How does spiral blade geometry affect rheological properties of 3D printing mixtures? What are effects of the rheological properties of 3D printing mixture on final extrudability? The discrete element model formed by particles bonded with liquid bridges is used to analyze the influence of 3D printer blade size, shape, and rotation speed on the extrudability of cement-based materials. It is demonstrated that effects of spiral blade geometry on rheological properties and resulting extrudability of 3D printing mixtures are considerable. The research results could be good references about geometry of spiral blades for 3D concrete printing industry. However, the microscopic time-varying constitutive model of particle bonding has not been generated in this paper. It might be one of the future research directions.</details>

### <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/closedaccess.svg"><img src="ico/wm/closedaccess.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture> <a href="https://github.com/dan-auer/3dcp.fyi/blob/main/dat/3dcp.fyi.bib#L110902-L110930" title="Get the BibTeX Entry"><picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/bibtex.svg"><img src="ico/wm/bibtex.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a> <a href="https://doi.org/10.14359/51734353" title="DOI" ><picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/doi.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/doi.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a> <a href="https://crossmark.crossref.org/dialog/?doi=10.14359/51734353&domain=pdf" title="Crossmark" ><picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/crossmark.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/crossmark.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a> <picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/blank.svg"><img src="ico/wm/blank.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture> Preparation and High-Velocity Impact Experiment for Three-Dimensional-Printed Concrete (2022-03)
Jiehang <b>Zhou</b>,
Longyu <b>Du</b>,
Jianzhong <b>Lai</b>,
Qiang <b>Wang</b>,
Saiyang <b>Dong</b>,
Yujie <b>Yang</b><br>Journal Article – ACI Materials Journal, Vol. 119, No. 2
<details><summary>Abstract</summary>Three-dimensional (3-D) printed concrete is a new technology for civil engineering. In this paper, 3-D printed concrete was prepared for a study on static and dynamic properties. The best fluidity of the concrete was researched and the optimization mixture ratio for better mechanical performance was discussed. The mechanical performances of the concrete were tested and the anisotropy phenomenon in 3-D printed concrete was found. The computed tomography (CT) scanning and imaging progress methods were used to discuss the reason for the phenomenon. The penetration experiments were carried out to research the dynamic performance of the 3-D printed concrete. The results of the penetration tests were compared with the empirical formulas. The Young formula was improved according to the results.</details>
<details><summary>Metrics</summary><img src="fig\zhou_du_lai_wang.2022.PaHVIEfTDPC.svg"></details><a href="https://scholar.google.com/scholar_lookup?title=Preparation%20and%20High-Velocity%20Impact%20Experiment%20for%20Three-Dimensional-Printed%20Concrete" title="Search on Google Scholar"><picture><source media="(prefers-color-scheme: dark)" srcset="ico/dm/googlescholar.svg" ><img src="ico/wm/googlescholar.svg" width="16" height="16"></picture></a>
